---
title: "Having problems installing Ubuntu on an Acer Aspire X1430 G"
date: 2014-08-07
forum: New to Ubuntu
---

### Post by Cindi_Marshall on 2014-08-07
Hello, I am a REAL newbie to Linux, as in I am taking the Intro to Linux class that is on edx and I have absolutely no clue what to do about this problem.

I have an Acer Aspire X1430G-UW30P running Windows 7.  I am trying to install Ubuntu 14.04.1.  I am able to mount the ISO file to a Virtual DVD Rom, and I can burn the files onto a DVD just fine.  But when I go in to rearrange my BIOS, I see and EFI selection and no matter what order I put the boot options in, it will read the DVD that is burnt, but then it goes right on to boot up in Windows 7.  Does anyone have any ideas that I can use?

Thank you so much in advance.

Cindi aka Too Sweet For Me (T2 diabetic using insulin)

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-07
Are you copying files not installing them. Just extracting files does not make a bootable DVD or flash drive.
Are you installing 64 bit version?

Is Windows 7 in BIOS or UEFI mode. Most Windows 7 systems are in BIOS mode with MBR partitioning, but a few were UEFI. You do want to be sure to install Ubuntu in the same boot mode as Windows.

Instructions for both Windows & Linux are on download page. Installation instructions at bottom of page link.
[http://www.ubuntu.com/download/desktop](http://www.ubuntu.com/download/desktop)

Some other instructions:
 Usb installer from Windows
[http://www.ubuntu.com/download/help/create-a-usb-stick-on-windows](http://www.ubuntu.com/download/help/create-a-usb-stick-on-windows)
Used rufus to create bootable USB and it worked! Used UUI and unetbootin before. 
[http://rufus.akeo.ie/](http://rufus.akeo.ie/)


Usb installer from Windows
 [http://www.ubuntu.com/download/help/create-a-usb-stick-on-windows](http://www.ubuntu.com/download/help/create-a-usb-stick-on-windows)
SOLVED!!! Used rufus to create bootable USB and it worked! I've tried UUI and unetbootin before. 
[http://rufus.akeo.ie/](http://rufus.akeo.ie/)

If system is UEFI, see all the links in my signature.

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-07
Those are the files, but just copying them to a DVD or flash drive does not make it bootable, except maybe with UEFI.

Windows only boots with UEFI from gpt partitioned drives and will have an efi partition.
Windows only boots from BIOS with MBR(msdos) partitioned drive and typically has a 100MB boot partition and the main install. 

From Ubuntu you can run this in terminal to see partitions and type.
sudo parted -l

If Windows 7 and in BIOS mode, most vendors managed to use all 4 primary partitions just to make it difficult to install another system. There are several workarounds for that if you have BIOS boot.

---

### Post by oldfred on 2014-08-07
First what partitions are used.
Post this from terminal in live installer:
sudo parted -l

You have to create Linux partitions for / (root) & swap at the minimum. Others are options and often /home is suggested. Also you may want a shared NTFS data partition as it is better not to write a lot into the Windows system partition. The installer will only create Linux partitions, so if you want a NTFS partition, use gparted in advance or leave some unallocated and create it afterwards with gparted.

Use Windows partition tools to shrink the NTFS partition and reboot to let it run chkdsk and update to its new size.
Do not create partitions with Windows. It may try to convert to dynamic partitions which do not work with Linux and even some Windows tools. 

       My laptop already has 4 primary partitions: how can I install Ubuntu?
[http://askubuntu.com/questions/149821/my-laptop-already-has-4-primary-partitions-how-can-i-install-ubuntu](http://askubuntu.com/questions/149821/my-laptop-already-has-4-primary-partitions-how-can-i-install-ubuntu)
Good advice on how to handle all four primary partitions used. - srs5694
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1686440](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=1686440)
Be sure to create recovery DVD(s) first. And a Windows repair CD.
HP tools partition discussion - similar for other vendor utility partitions:
[http://h30434.www3.hp.com/t5/Notebook-Hardware/Hp-Tools-Partion/td-p/228360](http://h30434.www3.hp.com/t5/Notebook-Hardware/Hp-Tools-Partion/td-p/228360)
